<p><b>Mallory Park</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Motor_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor racing">motor racing</a> circuit situated in the village of <a href="/wiki/Kirkby_Mallory" title="Kirkby Mallory">Kirkby Mallory</a>, just off the <a href="/wiki/A47_road" title="A47 road">A47</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinckley" title="Hinckley">Hinckley</a>, in central England. Originally used for <a href="/wiki/Dirt_track_racing#United_Kingdom" title="Dirt track racing">grass-track</a> until 1955, a new, basically oval hard-surfaced course was constructed for 1956, with a later extension forming a loop with a <a href="/wiki/Hairpin_turn" title="Hairpin turn">hairpin bend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-circuit_guide_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circuit_guide-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the car circuit measuring only 1.35 miles (2.173&#160;km) it is amongst the shortest permanent race circuits in the UK. However, chicanes introduced to reduce speeds in motorcycle events mean that the Superbike Circuit is now slightly longer, at 1.41 miles (2.269&#160;km). Shorter UK circuits are <a href="/wiki/Lydden_Race_Circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Lydden Race Circuit">Lydden Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brands_Hatch" title="Brands Hatch">Brands Hatch Indy circuit</a>, Scotland's <a href="/wiki/Knockhill_Racing_Circuit" title="Knockhill Racing Circuit">Knockhill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit" title="Silverstone Circuit">Silverstone's diminutive Stowe</a> circuit.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Circuit">The Circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: The Circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The circuit has a number of formations, founded on a basic one-mile oval, with the majority of configurations including the northerly extension to the tight, 180° <i>Shaw's Hairpin</i>. At the other end of the circuit lies the long right-hand <i>Gerard's Bend</i>. Gerard's is about a third of a mile long and turns through nearly 200°. It was named after local racing hero <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gerard" title="Bob Gerard">Bob Gerard</a>, who opened the newly reconstructed circuit on 25 April 1956. Unusually, there are a number of large lakes occupying approximately half of the circuit infield. Despite its short length and Shaw's Hairpin, the tightest corner of any UK track, (other than the hairpin on <a href="/wiki/Cadwell_Park" title="Cadwell Park">Cadwell Park</a>'s short circuit,) Mallory is a fast circuit. To reduce speeds for motorcycle racing a pair of chicanes have been introduced, together with a revised exit to Gerard's. <i>Edwina's</i> was added toward the end of the straight following Gerard's, named after former managing director of the circuit Edwina Overend, and the <i>Bus Stop Chicane</i> on the descent to the sweeping left kink, the <i>Devil's Elbow</i>, a blind, downhill, <a href="/wiki/Off-camber_corner" class="mw-redirect" title="Off-camber corner">off camber</a> left-hander before the start–finish line on <i>Kirkby Straight</i>. In 2003 a new complex was added toward the end of Gerard's curve. This sequence of bends was designed to reduce speeds on entry to Edwina's, and to prevent motorcycles from colliding as they jockey for position into the chicane.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mallory Park does not have any true permanent garage facilities, although there are a handful of open garages in the pitlane.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_.E2.80.93_1950s">Origins – 1950s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Origins – 1950s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg/200px-Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg/300px-Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg/400px-Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mallory_Park_Trackday.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Motorcycle riders passing through the John Cooper Esses, taking part in a circuit <a href="/wiki/Track_day" title="Track day">track day</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The estate at Mallory Park has many historical connections, the oldest being the unique Anglo-Saxons defended moat which is now known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kirkby_Moats&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kirkby Moats (page does not exist)">Kirkby Moats</a>, while a Roman road passes through the estate. Fast forward to the 18th century, when in 1762, Sir <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleoberry_Noel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cleoberry Noel (page does not exist)">Cleoberry Noel</a> became Viscount Wentworth, the title descended on the distaff side. <a href="/wiki/Lord_Byron" title="Lord Byron">Lord Byron</a> married into the Wentworth family and it is said on his visits to Mallory, he wrote beneath the shade of the Lebanon cedar tree which still stands in the grounds of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kirkby_Hall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kirkby Hall (page does not exist)">Kirkby Hall</a>. The last occupant of Kirkby Hall was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Herbert_Clarkson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Herbert Clarkson (page does not exist)">Herbert Clarkson</a> who died in 1941, when it was sold.</p>
<p>During the Second World War, the circuit started life Royal Air Force Station Kirkby Mallory, a standby landing ground (SLG) during WWII and closed in 1947. The hall was a large house which was demolished in 1952, leaving only the stable block and the coach house which now forms the circuit offices, workshops, hotel, pub and restaurant.</p>
<p>The estate of 300 acres was sold by auction in 1953 and was bought by a Mr. Moult of Derby who planned to have horse racing on the disused pony trotting track. Following the war, Mallory became a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pony_trotting&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pony trotting (page does not exist)">pony trotting</a> circuit in the late 1940s, which defined the outline of the oval track still in use today. After the financial collapse of the equestrian club responsible for the circuit (Kirkby Mallory Racing Association), the track was hired by various motorcycle clubs for grass track motorcycle and motorcycle sidecar racing. For example, between September 1949 until 1954, the Leicester Query Motorcycle Club held grass track races. In 1955, the estate was purchased by Clive Wormleighton, under whose influence, the present tarmac was constructed at a cost of £60,000 in 1956. Upon completion of the building work, a circuit test was held on 26 April, when local Grand Prix driver <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gerard" title="Bob Gerard">Bob Gerard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Cann" title="Maurice Cann">Maurice Cann</a> respectively conducted a <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Car_Company" title="Cooper Car Company">Cooper</a>-Bristol Formula Two car and a <a href="/wiki/Moto_Guzzi" title="Moto Guzzi">Moto Guzzi</a> motorcycle around the track, Gerald managing an 81&#160;mph lap.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The very first race was held on 29 April, when the Leicester Query Club organised a motorcycle meeting. A large crowd in excess of 20,000 spectators attended the <i>Grand Opening</i> event on 13 May 1956. 248 riders arrived in Leicestershire for this meeting, which saw <a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Salter_(motorcycle_racer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="George Salter (motorcycle racer) (page does not exist)">George Salter</a> set the first lap record at a speed of 84.08&#160;mph, riding a <a href="/wiki/Norton_Motorcycle_Company" title="Norton Motorcycle Company">Norton</a> bike. Cars first appeared at the Whit Monday meeting, in event being organised by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nottingham_Sports_Car_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nottingham Sports Car Club (page does not exist)">Nottingham Sports Car Club</a>. The first car race victory went to D. Rees in an Austin.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg/220px-Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg/330px-Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg/440px-Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Chapman_statue_Mallory_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A statue of Lotus Cars and Team Lotus founder Colin Chapman, at the Hairpin Gate into the Mallory Park motor racing circuit</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many famous racing stars have raced at Mallory over the years, indeed a young <a href="/wiki/John_Surtees" title="John Surtees">John Surtees</a> raced against his father, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_Surtees_(motorcycle_racer)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jack Surtees (motorcycle racer) (page does not exist)">Jack Surtees</a>. While Jack was a successfully grass track racer at Mallory, John went on to be only World Champion on both two and four wheels.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Famous competitors who have raced at Mallory, include <a href="/wiki/John_Surtees" title="John Surtees">John Surtees</a> who won the first ‘<a href="/wiki/Mallory_Park_Race_of_the_Year" title="Mallory Park Race of the Year">Race of the Year</a>’ in 1958. While, the 1960 race, saw <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hailwood" title="Mike Hailwood">Mike Hailwood</a> win and set a new lap record of 89&#160;mph. Both Hailwood and Surtees, along with Jim Clark and Colin Chapman are commemorated with Statues at the front gate. Around this time, Clive Wormleighton added the lakes, which were formed by adding the sluice gate across the Brook.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mallorypark.co.uk_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mallorypark.co.uk-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Clive Wormleighton continued to run the circuit very successfully until 1962 when ownership passed to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Grovewood_Securities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Grovewood Securities (page does not exist)">Grovewood Securities</a> in the July, the previous owner remaining in a consultancy capacity until the end of September. Before this, on 11 June 1962 Mallory Park saw it first non-championship Formula One (<i><a href="/wiki/1962_International_2000_Guineas" title="1962 International 2000 Guineas">International 2000 Guineas</a></i>) race, won by <a href="/wiki/John_Surtees" title="John Surtees">John Surtees</a> aboard a <a href="/wiki/Lola_Cars" title="Lola Cars">Lola</a> <a href="/wiki/Lola_Mk4" title="Lola Mk4">Mk4</a> from the privately entered Lotuses of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brabham" title="Jack Brabham">Jack Brabham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graham_Hill" title="Graham Hill">Graham Hill</a>. Surtees was now a major race winner at Mallory on both 2 and 4 wheels.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the next two years, a considerable amount of money was spent on Mallory with the building of new spectator stands and a new commentators’ press and timekeepers’ boxes. Further developments took place raising the standard of the track. Crowd grew and in 1962, over 50,000 people paid to see the <i>Post TT International</i> Motor Cycle meeting, when Mike Hailwood won, improving the lap record to 91.70&#160;mph. This led to it <i><a href="/wiki/Mallory_Park_Race_of_the_Year" title="Mallory Park Race of the Year">Race of the Year</a></i> and <i>Sidecar race of the Year</i> being sponsored by <i>the Daily Mail</i>. Under the control of Grovewood Securities, Mallory enjoyed its golden days in the 1960s and 1970s with some of the greatest names in motorsport competing there. Amongst these, a young Austrian who arrived for the Whit Sunday meeting in 1964, for his first race in England in a new <a href="/wiki/Formula_Two" title="Formula Two">Formula Two</a> <a href="/wiki/Brabham" title="Brabham">Brabham</a> – <a href="/wiki/Jochen_Rindt" title="Jochen Rindt">Jochen Rindt</a>. He asked <a href="/wiki/Denny_Hulme" title="Denny Hulme">Denny Hulme</a> if he could follow him round to learn the circuit and then proceeded to set fastest time in qualifying; despite being delayed in the race, he finished third behind the reigning World Champion, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Clark" title="Jim Clark">Jim Clark</a> and his experienced team-mate <a href="/wiki/Peter_Arundell" title="Peter Arundell">Peter Arundell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mallorypark.co.uk_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mallorypark.co.uk-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Throughout the Sixties and Seventies, the circuit hosted almost every major British car and bike championship. However, on occasions there were European Championship events. For example, 12 March 1972, saw FIA <a href="/wiki/European_Formula_Two_Championship" title="European Formula Two Championship">European Formula Two Championship</a>, with Dave Morgan winning in his Reeves Racing <a href="/wiki/Brabham" title="Brabham">Brabham</a>-<a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a> BT38, from the future Ferrari pairing of <a href="/wiki/Niki_Lauda" title="Niki Lauda">Niki Lauda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Reutemann" title="Carlos Reutemann">Carlos Reutemann</a>.</p>
<p>1970 saw Mallory used as a venue for cycle racing with the <a href="/wiki/1970_UCI_Road_World_Championships" title="1970 UCI Road World Championships">World road race championships</a> being run on a road course starting and finishing at Mallory and incorporating the circuit (reversed) each lap. The professional event was won by ill-fated Belgian <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Monser%C3%A9" title="Jean-Pierre Monseré">Jean-Pierre Monseré</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Formula Two returned again 1973, this time Morgan could only finish third. The victor was Frenchman, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Jarier" title="Jean-Pierre Jarier">Jean-Pierre Jarier</a> in his works <a href="/wiki/March_Engineering" title="March Engineering">March</a>-<a href="/wiki/BMW_in_motorsport" title="BMW in motorsport">BMW</a> 732. Second was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dave_McConnell_(racing_driver)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dave McConnell (racing driver) (page does not exist)">Dave McConnell</a>.</p>
<p>After a little over 20 years the owners of Mallory Park decided that enough was enough and offered the estate for sale; no doubt the expense of bringing <a href="/wiki/Brands_Hatch" title="Brands Hatch">Brands Hatch</a> (which Grovewood also owned) up to current Grand Prix standards had some effort on the decision and the re-opening of <a href="/wiki/Donington_Park" title="Donington Park">Donington Park</a>, which was only some 20 miles away, may have influenced the decision. Whatever the reasons, Mallory was once more on the market but, reportedly with a restriction in its future use for motor sport on its future use for motor racing, although planning permission had been obtained for the erection of 30 dwelling on the estate.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, famously the <a href="/wiki/Bay_City_Rollers" title="Bay City Rollers">Bay City Rollers</a> tartan army played a concert during a BBC-organised 'Fun Day' on 18 May 1975, on a stage specifically constructed in the middle of the lake.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s_and_onwards">1980s and onwards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1980s and onwards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG/200px-Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG" width="200" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG/300px-Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG/400px-Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1016" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotus_Elite_at_Mallory_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Elite" title="Lotus Elite">Lotus Elite</a> cornering on a <a href="/wiki/Hairpin_turn" title="Hairpin turn">hairpin</a> in November 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Enter a very determined lady, Edwina Overend, who was the competitions secretary of the Midlands Centre of the <a href="/wiki/British_Racing_and_Sports_Car_Club" title="British Racing and Sports Car Club">British Racing and Sports Car Club</a> (BRSCC). As the time passed and the 1982 season drew to its close, the expected cessation of racing at Mallory loomed large and various time wasters had come and gone, Overend approached <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chris_Meek_(racing_driver)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chris Meek (racing driver) (page does not exist)">Chris Meek</a> with a view to his purchasing the estate. Meek was a well-known racing driver and businessman who effected the purchase late in 1982, and reopened the circuit on 29 May 1983, the first race of the new era being organised by the <a href="/wiki/750_Motor_Club" title="750 Motor Club">750 Motor Club</a>. There was no interruption to the programme and Mallory went from strength to strength, apart from a hiccup from in December 1985 when the local borough council served a Noise Nuisance Order which restricted use of the circuit to 40 days a year. On Sundays there is an absolute curfew and no racing engines must be run after 6 pm.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mallory Park has hosted all major motor racing formulae to be contested in post-war England – <a href="/wiki/European_Formula_Two_Championship" title="European Formula Two Championship">European Formula Two Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Formula_One_Series" title="British Formula One Series">British Formula One Series</a>, <a href="/wiki/Group_7_(racing)" title="Group 7 (racing)">Group 7</a> sport cars, European <a href="/wiki/Formula_5000" title="Formula 5000">Formula 5000</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Formula_Three_Championship" title="British Formula Three Championship">British Formula Three Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">British Saloon Car Championship</a>. In the 1981 programme the name of <a href="/wiki/Damon_Hill" title="Damon Hill">Damon Hill</a> appears as one of the ‘Ams’ in the <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_RD350" title="Yamaha RD350">Yamaha RD350</a> Pro-Am series.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Annually in October, The Festival of Sidecars takes place. No solo machines compete, but <a href="/wiki/Sidecar" title="Sidecar">sidecars</a> of all categories are entered, including three-wheelers such as those made by the <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Motor_Company" title="Morgan Motor Company">Morgan Motor Company</a>.</p>
<p>From the mid-1990s, the BRSCC promoted EuroCars, V6 and V8 saloon-outline cars which had graduated from the stock car circuits. At Mallory Park, they ran anticlockwise on the oval circuit.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG/200px-Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG/300px-Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG/400px-Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1074" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lola_T70_Spyder_Mallory_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Lola_T70" title="Lola T70">Lola T70</a> Spyder sports car, on test at Mallory Park, October 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The history of the 100&#160;mph lap at the Leicestershire circuit is interesting; the first one was a long time coming, for it was not until 1966 that it finally happened when on 29 May, Denny Hulme took a <a href="/wiki/Lola_T70" title="Lola T70">Lola T70</a> round in 47.6sec at a speed of 102.10&#160;mph. Two years later, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Roy_Pike&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Roy Pike (page does not exist)">Roy Pike</a> established the first Formula Three 100&#160;mph lap in a Titan, which he took round in 48sec (101.25&#160;mph). With coming of the large capacity single-seater like the Formula 5000 and Formula One cars, the outright record continue to fall until, in 1979, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Zunino" title="Ricardo Zunino">Ricardo Zunino</a> took an <a href="/wiki/Arrows_Grand_Prix_International" title="Arrows Grand Prix International">Arrows</a> <a href="/wiki/Arrows_A1" title="Arrows A1">A1</a> round in 40.065sec at an incredible 121.32&#160;mph. 22 years after the 100&#160;mph late, <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Sospiri" title="Vincenzo Sospiri">Vincenzo Sospiri</a> established the first such lap in a <a href="/wiki/Formula_Ford" title="Formula Ford">Formula Ford</a> when he drove a <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen" title="Van Diemen">Van Diemen</a> RF88 at 100.41&#160;mph in 48.44sec.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the end of the 20th Century, the outright lap record on the full circuit, which still stands to the credit of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johan_Rajam%C3%A4ki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Johan Rajamäki (page does not exist)">Johan Rajamäki</a>, driving a Formula One <a href="/wiki/Footwork_Arrows" title="Footwork Arrows">Footwork-Judd</a> <a href="/wiki/Footwork_FA13" title="Footwork FA13">FA13</a> in the BOSS Formula at 127.12 in 38.23secs. it was set on 5 May 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the oval circuit, the record has stood since May 1995, the credit of a V6 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a> Eurocar of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ian_Fewings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ian Fewings (page does not exist)">Ian Fewings</a> at 106.51&#160;mph in 33.84sec.<sup id="cite_ref-Swinger_3-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swinger-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>While on two wheels, the full lap record was set during the 2008 ‘<a href="/wiki/Mallory_Park_Race_of_the_Year" title="Mallory Park Race of the Year">Race of the year</a>’ at 51.271secs, a speed of 97.599&#160;mph, by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Sykes" title="Tom Sykes">Tom Sykes</a> abroad a 1300cc Suzuki.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motocross_Circuit">Motocross Circuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Motocross Circuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg/200px-Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg/300px-Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg/400px-Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Cairoli_ITA_FMI_Yamaha_FIM_MX_Mallory_Park_2008_R6a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tony_Cairoli" title="Tony Cairoli">Antonio Cairoli</a>, riding a FMI <a href="/wiki/Yamaha_YZ450F" title="Yamaha YZ450F">Yamaha YZ450F</a>, winning the FIM MX2 round at Mallory Park 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Adjacent to the road course is a purpose-built <a href="/wiki/Motocross" title="Motocross">motocross</a> circuit which played host to the Grand Prix of Great Britain in 2008. The event was being organised by off-road promotions company RHL, who originally planned to use the former Grand Prix circuit at <a href="/wiki/Foxhill_motocross_circuit" title="Foxhill motocross circuit">Foxhill</a>, near Swindon, until it became apparent that the infrastructure at the Wiltshire venue would not be sufficient for such a high-profile event.</p>
<p>The event was seen as a success by fans, with over 30,000 fans in attendance over the weekend. However, the Grand Prix only returned once more in 2009.</p>
<p>The circuit has been unused since late 2013 and has fallen into disuse. Motocross activities ended due to noise concerns and, in the interests of improving relations with the local community, the new owners of the circuit have no plans to recommence Motocross.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_Race_Results">Major Race Results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Major Race Results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formula_One_Non-World_Championship_races">Formula One Non-World Championship races</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Formula One Non-World Championship races">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Formula_5000_Championship">European Formula 5000 Championship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mallory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: European Formula 5000 Championship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The BRSCC's <a href="/wiki/European_Formula_5000_Championship" title="European Formula 5000 Championship">European Formula 5000 Championship</a>, organised in the UK but taking in events across Europe, was first contested in 1969. The title sponsorship moved from Guards to Rothmans to Shellsport before the series let in F1, F2 and F. Atlantic cars for 1976.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG/220px-Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG/330px-Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG/440px-Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="890" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lola_T332_Mallory_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Interscope-liveried <a href="/wiki/Lola_T332" title="Lola T332">Lola T332</a> Formula 5000 car rounds the hairpin at Mallory Park, October 2009.</div>
</div>
